### Things to do in the Marina

![](https://i.imgur.com/jNedsSH.jpeg)

There’s so much to do in The Marina but I’d say the main things are to…

- Hit the parks and hangout on the lawns of Crissy Field, Marina Green, Presidio Tunnel Tops, and Fort Mason
- Go shopping on both Chestnut and Union Street
- Take in the epic views of the Golden Gate Bridge from [a cruise along the ocean](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=3965&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.getyourguide.com%2Fsan-francisco-l61%2F&trs=299090&journey_id=JgzvPiaiwQ-WcZShJdbtw&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner ""), Fort Point National Historic Site, and/or the Golden Gate Overlook
- Dine at top-rated restaurants like [Little Original Joe’s](https://www.littleoriginaljoes.com/ ""), [Mamanoko](https://www.mamanokosf.com/ ""), and more.
- Sip on handcrafted cocktails from Left Door (where we had our wedding reception), Wilder, and Balboa Café (known for their famous espressotinis)

Ps. For a complete list of my favorite eats, [head to my local’s guide on how to spend 3 perfect days in San Francisco!](https://discoveroverthere.com/3-day-san-francisco-itinerary/ "")

The Marina has plenty to do, but more importantly, **this is where the locals actually hang out.**

**Main Takeaway:** The Marina is not only one of San Francisco’s trendiest neighborhoods but also one of the safest areas in San Francisco to stay. Stay here for charming coffee shops, great shopping, epic Golden Gate Bridge views, and easy access to Marin and Sausalito. It’s also one of the safest picks when deciding where to stay in San Francisco, especially for solo travelers.

## Where to Stay in San Francisco: Union Square

![](https://i.imgur.com/u9XsLPs.jpeg)

Okay well obviously I’m going to talk about Union Square next since it’s a great location for a wide range of hotel types. Union Square is basically the go-to spot for first-time visitors, and honestly, I get why. It’s packed with hotels, nonstop shopping, cocktail bars, theaters, and some of the best restaurants in the city.

During the day, you can hop from designer boutiques to local shops, and by night, the area is buzzing with rooftop bars, craft cocktail spots, and top-tier dining. Plus, it’s a major transit hub, so getting around the city is a breeze. It’s also generally safe. Yes it’s _technically_ a neighboring area to the Tenderloin which is the “sketchy” part of town but you’ll be completely fine in the center of Union Square.

In the FAQ section below, I’ll give you exactly which streets and areas to avoid in San Francisco. But believe me, Union Square is **NOT** one of them!

If you want to be in the middle of all the action with everything at your doorstep, Union Square is a solid choice.

### Things to do in Union Square

![](https://i.imgur.com/VdP6KLt.jpeg)

Since Union Square is San Francisco’s shopping, dining, and entertainment scene — that means it’s pretty much always packed with things to do year-round.

You’ll want to take some photos at the Dewey Monument and heart sculptures, then explore high-end boutiques, department stores, and local shops lining the square. Don’t miss the San Francisco cable car turnaround at the end of Powell Street, where you can hop on a $8 historic ride up to Nob Hill or Fisherman’s Wharf.

If you’re in SF during the holidays, you _have_ to check out the Union Square ice rink. The whole square transforms into a festive wonderland with a giant skating rink and an even bigger Christmas tree. Oh, and they recently added [Let’s Glow SF](https://downtownsf.org/things-to-do/lets-glow-sf ""), a pretty cool light show that projects massive art displays onto downtown buildings every night during the holiday season.

One of the best things you can do is hit up a [food tour in Chinatown](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=3965&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.getyourguide.com%2Fsan-francisco-l61%2Fculinary-walking-tour-of-chinatown-t9463%2F%3Franking_uuid%3Dde6453b4-a42f-4f5b-a3a7-e47f0cd293cb&trs=299090&journey_id=jo8276kSa90eF6eiNajHb&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner ""). It’s so close and totally worth it. I always tell my friends visiting for the first time to check out [this particular one](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=3965&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.getyourguide.com%2Fsan-francisco-l61%2Fculinary-walking-tour-of-chinatown-t9463%2F%3Franking_uuid%3Dde6453b4-a42f-4f5b-a3a7-e47f0cd293cb&trs=299090&journey_id=H4Qz6_7rdYhmCK4QIw8Cx&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") because I think they stop at all the best places. Like the Golden Gate Fortune Cookie Factory 🥠🥠🥠

For my favorite hidden gem, head inside the recently renovated [Westin St. Francis](https://tripadvisor.tpk.lu/kp0OZDNV?trs=299090&journey_id=NbYlIQqH1BxG5OOIpOUSd&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_short&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") and check out the [Chateau Montelena Tasting Room](http://e/ ""), where you can sip world-class Napa Valley wines without ever leaving the city.

**Main Takeaway:** If you want to be in the heart of San Francisco’s action, Union Square is the place to stay. With endless shopping, top-tier restaurants, and easy access to public transit (including the iconic cable cars), it’s a prime spot for first-time visitors.

## Where to Stay in San Francisco: Nob Hill

![](https://i.imgur.com/b3W9VJr.jpeg)

Alright, you might start to think this article’s a little biased towards neighborhoods I’ve lived in or currently live in…and you’d be right!

But hey, I like to live in nice, clean, and safe parts of San Francisco, which is exactly why I’m all about Nob Hill.

Whether it’s your first time or your 7th time visiting, this neighborhood is perfect for anyone who wants a blend of history, charm, and luxury. Or for anyone who enjoys getting their a\*\* kicked by all of the crazy hills.

My favorite part about Nob Hill is that you’ll get stunning views of the city, plus a mix of high-end hotels, cozy cafes, underrated Italian restaurants, and historic landmarks like Grace Cathedral, The Masonic, The Cable Car Museum, and Huntington Park. Which just happens to be where you’ll find my dog and I almost every evening after work 🐶

It’s peaceful, central, and hands down one of the best places to stay in SF.

So yeah, maybe I’m a little biased, but Nob Hill really does have it all 😺

### Where to stay in San Francisco’s Nob Hill: Top boutique hotel picks

- [Nob Hill Hotel —](https://tripadvisor.tpk.lu/xRY7x1Sw?trs=299090&journey_id=fK_8rUKl405RQcxY3oeKZ&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_short&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") There’s not a ton of hotel options in proper Nob Hill which is why [Nob Hill Hotel](https://emrldtp.com/re?campaign_id=594&marker=522542&p=8645&trs=299090&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.expedia.com%2Fh118353.Hotel-Information%3Fadults%3D2%26afflid%3D1011lAmhIbo7%26clickref%3D1011lAmhIbo7%26destination%3DSan%2BFrancisco%252C%2BCA%252C%2BUSA%26my_ad%3DAFF.US.DIRECT.PHG.1011l45458.0%26numRoom%3D1%26ref_id%3D1011lAmhIbo7&product_type=linkswitcher&journey_id=vZRsHSwpsDRpnJkKopqbd&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&install_type=partner "") holds a special place in my heart. ### Things to do in Nob Hill

![](https://i.imgur.com/cGPUb90.jpeg)

I mentioned some of the best things to do in Nob Hill already but definitely want to hi-light both Grace Cathedral and The Cable Car Museum. Grace Cathedral is a stunning Gothic-style cathedral known for its beautiful stained glass, labyrinth walks, and breathtaking interior. Sometimes they even hold “yoga by candlelight” inside the church and it’s seriously a transformational experience.

Then there’s [The Cable Car Museum](https://www.cablecarmuseum.org/ "") which is kinda quirky but I love it. It’s definitely a must-visit for history buffs (like myself) as it gives you a behind-the-scenes look at how SF’s cable cars work. Spoiler: they’re manual AF and I never know how the workers do it for 8+ hours a day.

As for restaurants and dining, there’s **SO MANY** good hidden gems. There’s [Nob Hill Cafe](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=4456&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.tripadvisor.com%2FRestaurant_Review-g60713-d353941-Reviews-Nob_Hill_Cafe-San_Francisco_California.html&trs=299090&journey_id=6MFVM1LoItTzPCFUeuCVs&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") which is an iconic Italian restaurant, [Key Klub](https://www.keyklubsf.com/ "") which serves natural wine, and [Liholiho Yacht Club](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=4456&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.tripadvisor.com%2FRestaurant_Review-g60713-d7627146-Reviews-Liholiho_Yacht_Club-San_Francisco_California.html&trs=299090&journey_id=tvKjYs3pEQvmjCrL1yqi_&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner ""). Where aloha meets San Francisco at this popular dinner spot that serves Hawaiian, Californian, and Asian-inspired dishes. 🍙

_Ps. If you’re craving a bomb burrito but don’t feel like making the trek to the Mission District, head to El Super Burrito on Polk Street in Nob Hill. It’s a total hidden gem. Known for its massive portions and authentic flavors, this spot will satisfy your burrito cravings without the tourists 🌯_

**Main Takeaway**: Nob Hill is where history, luxury, and stunning views come together. If you want a **safe,** elegant neighborhood with renowned hotels, classic San Francisco charm, and easy access to the rest of the city, this is the place to stay.

## Where to Stay in San Francisco: Russian Hill

![](https://i.imgur.com/wpDDSZa.jpeg)

Just down the hill from Nob Hill (and up another — because, well, welcome to San Francisco), Russian Hill is a mostly residential neighborhood packed with scenic streets, charming cafes, and, of course, the iconic Lombard Street, aka the world’s most famous crooked road.

If you’re deciding where to stay in San Francisco and want classic city charm with a quieter feel, this area is a gem.

### Where to stay in San Francisco’s Russian Hill: Top boutique hotel picks

- [Fairmont Heritage Place, Ghirardelli Square —](https://tripadvisor.tpk.lu/a7BFHfKe?trs=299090&journey_id=0K7ylxt1SY7ZCJIU2Bo1K&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_short&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") There’s really only one **true** hotel in Russian Hill and that’s the Fairmont Heritage Place. Located right next to Ghiradelli Square, this hotel is definitely considered a luxury stay. All of the rooms are suites with waterfront views and easy access to Fisherman’s Wharf. It’s perfect if you want a high-end stay with home-like comfort. Plus, you’re literally steps away from endless chocolate. [Book via Booking.com](https://booking.tpk.lu/JXl8VRTQ?trs=299090&journey_id=c-I3TeLZNyZ_rzjsDEj7O&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_short&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner) [Book via Expedia](https://expedia.tpk.lu/9l72Ku3N?trs=299090&journey_id=ImpOwfslpce6kFqwJTvfS&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_short&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner)

### Things to do in Russian Hill

![](https://i.imgur.com/x0a79BH.jpeg)

Given that it’s mostly a residential area, there’s not a ton of major attractions besides Lombard Street. Which is why you know that it’s definitely a safe place to stay since a lot of locals live nearby. However, there’s Francisco Park, which is a huge bi-level park that overlooks the bay, that’s worth checking out.

There’s also some of my favorite places to eat such as [Elephant Sushi](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=4456&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.tripadvisor.com%2FRestaurant_Review-g60713-d6533570-Reviews-Elephant_Sushi-San_Francisco_California.html&trs=299090&journey_id=qX-aZlwg7YC3zDWKhLK7j&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner ""), [Seven Hills](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=4456&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.tripadvisor.com%2FRestaurant_Review-g60713-d1999071-Reviews-Seven_Hills-San_Francisco_California.html&trs=299090&journey_id=J8Vxk2FdQ1met1WFqZOMo&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner ""), [Saru Handroll Bar](https://www.yelp.com/biz/saru-handroll-bar-san-francisco-2 ""), and [Leopold’s.](https://www.yelp.com/biz/leopolds-san-francisco-2 "") You also can’t miss [Swensen’s](https://swensensofsf.com/ "") for a sweet treat after dinner 🍦

**Main Takeaway**: Russian Hill is one of the safest areas in San Francisco to stay, with classic charm, stunning views, quiet residential streets, and easy access to Lombard Street, North Beach, and the waterfront. If you’re figuring out where to stay in San Francisco and want somewhere walkable, charming, and super local, this area is one of the safest and best choices.

## Where to Stay in San Francisco: Pacific Heights (Pac Heights)

![](https://i.imgur.com/Ke0fExJ.jpeg)

Alright, I promise. This is the last of the hills. Pacific Heights aka Pac Heights is one of SF’s most picturesque (and upscale) neighborhoods, stretching from the edge of Japantown all the way down to the Richmond District.

Think grand mansions, tree-lined streets, and some of the best views in the city. Especially from Lafayette Park (my dog’s 2nd home) and the famous Lyon Street Steps.

While it’s mostly residential, it’s home to some fantastic boutique shopping and dining along Fillmore Street, plus it puts you within easy reach of both downtown and the quieter western neighborhoods.

If you want a beautiful, safe, and peaceful place to stay with a mix of historic charm and local vibes, Pacific Heights is a solid choice.

You’ll kinda feel like you’re stepping into your Grandma’s house here but I think that’s part of the charm! - [Hotel Drisco —](https://tripadvisor.tpk.lu/9Q1QPO7g?trs=299090&journey_id=d8_iMKVfleXpYd5UorXGA&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_short&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") Easily one of the most luxurious hotels in the city (which makes sense considering the wealthiest of the wealthy all live in Pac Heights). [Hotel Drisco](https://tripadvisor.tpk.lu/9Q1QPO7g?trs=299090&journey_id=RVmNW2HkyvET0IKOdwvmq&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_short&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") is definitely a 5-star property with panoramic views of the bridge and an onsite spa. Tbh, I always thought famous people would stay here but most of them end up staying at The Fairmont in Nob Hill. But you can’t go wrong with any of these hotels. ### Things to do in Pacific Heights (Pac Heights)

![](https://i.imgur.com/6R7mtz1.jpeg)

Since Pac Heights is pretty spread out, I’d suggest spending more time near Japantown and closer to Fillmore Street. The rest is mostly residential.

You can take a stroll through Lafayette Park for some of the best views of the Golden Gate Bridge and San Francisco Bay, or explore the beautiful Alamo Square for classic photo ops with the famous Painted Ladies.

For shopping and dining, you’ll want to head down to Fillmore Street. It’s a big, long street filled with a mix of brand names (Lululemon, Sezane, Kiehl’s, etc) and smaller boutiques. My favorite places to eat/drink on Fillmore are [The Tailor’s Son](https://www.thetailorssonsf.com/ ""), [The Snug](https://www.thesnugsf.com/ ""), and [State Bird Provisions](https://www.statebirdsf.com/ "") (super casual 1 Michelin Star restaurant).

You can check out my full review of [The Tailor’s Son](https://discoveroverthere.com/10-exceptional-italian-restaurants-in-san-francisco/ "") in my list of [Top 10 Italian restaurants in San Francisco!](https://discoveroverthere.com/10-exceptional-italian-restaurants-in-san-francisco/ "")

**Main Takeaway**: I’d say staying in Pac Heights is pretty similar to staying in Russian Hill. It’s safe, peaceful, and more upscale with easy access to some notable sights, beautiful parks, and boutique shops.

## Where to Stay in San Francisco: Fisherman’s Wharf

![](https://i.imgur.com/tWfsQsG.jpeg)

If you’re staying in Fisherman’s Wharf, get ready for tourist-central vibes. Think tons of souvenir shops, big-chain stores, and seafood stalls where you can grab a quick bite from the bay. They **do** make bread bowls here in the shape of animals so that’s a plus at least.

Fisherman’s Wharf is obviously not where the locals hang, but it’s the best spot if you want to be close to Pier 39, Ghirardelli Square, and the adorable sea lions at Aquatic Park.

Just be warned that it’s a bit chaotic but there’s a great selection of hotels and no shortage of things to do and see if you’re into the full SF tourist experience.

### Where to stay in San Francisco’s Fisherman’s Wharf: Top boutique hotel picks

- [Hotel Riu Plaza Fisherman’s Wharf —](https://tripadvisor.tpk.lu/hED7cY8X?trs=299090&journey_id=OzUhpG-OTNtzfjHhrvwh_&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_short&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") A modern, spacious hotel just steps from Pier 39 and the waterfront, offering comfy rooms, a heated outdoor pool, and free breakfast — because sightseeing on an empty stomach is not the move. ### Things to do in Fisherman’s Wharf

![](https://i.imgur.com/iQTUxf1.jpeg)

Like I mentioned earlier, Fisherman’s Wharf is all about the touristy fun so you can’t be mad about it if you’re planning to stay here.

You’ve got the classic Pier 39 with its candy shops and sea lions. Yes, the sea lions are a must-see. And a bunch of fresh seafood joints to hit up (get that clam chowder in a turtle-shaped sourdough bowl).

Don’t forget Ghirardelli Square for chocolate and a make-your-own ice cream sundae, or hop on a boat to check out [Alcatraz](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=3965&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.getyourguide.com%2Falcatraz-l535%2F&trs=299090&journey_id=D8hGo_XSG1S8aVmfTiglh&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner ""). Even as a local, I’ll head to [Alcatraz](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=3965&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.getyourguide.com%2Falcatraz-l535%2F&trs=299090&journey_id=Q_sOPPnpLmElfQI6_zKDb&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") at least once every couple years when I’m showing people around. It’s touristy but also the history is fascinating.

There’s also a really [fun night tour of Alcatraz](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=3965&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.getyourguide.com%2Fsan-francisco-l61%2Fsan-francisco-alcatraz-ticket-ferry-self-guided-app-t822893%2F%3Franking_uuid%3D6a30ea38-65a3-4b21-8bd8-289e4d634fc8&trs=299090&journey_id=jNk0YVZBkMFht8fg_3FaD&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") where you get to visit the prison at night. It’s a bit creepy but totally worth it. Plus, the views of the city from across the way are STUNNING, making it one of the safest places to stay in San Francisco for a memorable experience.

**Main Takeaway**: Fisherman’s Wharf is a great place to stay if you don’t mind being in tourist central. It’s known to be safe, and the area is packed with souvenir shops, local attractions, and top-rated seafood 🦀

## Where to Stay in San Francisco: Financial District (FIDI)

![](https://i.imgur.com/mhOWEPh.jpeg)

This area’s mostly for my business travelers and/or conference folks but there are some incredible hotels in downtown San Francisco that I would totally stay in even if you’re not traveling for work. FIDI is San Francisco’s main financial district but it also extends into parts of Soma (south of Market street) and The Embarcadero (the main road along the water).

Similar to most cities, this area is commonly referred to as “downtown SF” 🙂

### Where to stay in San Francisco’s Financial District (FIDI): Top boutique hotel picks

The rooms are small here but the value for money is fantastic. I actually use to stay here all the time as a flight attendant with American Airlines! (No clue if it’s still used as a crew hotel anymore or not but it was a great place to stay overnight). ### Things to do in Financial District (FIDI)

![](https://i.imgur.com/mLMhfXC.jpeg)

Surprisingly FIDI isn’t just for business travelers. It’s got some serious personality and some beautiful cityscapes once you find the right spots. You’ve got the [Transamerica Pyramid](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=4456&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.tripadvisor.com%2FAttraction_Review-g60713-d144408-Reviews-Transamerica_Pyramid-San_Francisco_California.html&trs=299090&journey_id=dXW87UGM1qFcb-9rSR7tv&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") looming overhead, which is one of San Francisco’s most recognizable landmarks.

Completed in 1972, this triangle-shaped building was once the tallest in the city and still stands as a symbol of modern architecture. While you can’t exactly wander up to the top (unless you’re lucky enough to work there), the building’s unique shape and striking presence make it a must-see from almost every corner of downtown.

Just down the road, you’ve got the SFMOMA museum and the historic Ferry Building for delicious eats.

The [Ferry Building](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=4456&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.tripadvisor.com%2FAttraction_Review-g60713-d103851-Reviews-Ferry_Building_Marketplace-San_Francisco_California.html&trs=299090&journey_id=TwCJXOy3hQ0Ari-uUtEER&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") is a foodie paradise and one of San Francisco’s best spots for local eats, waterfront views, and a little history. Originally built in 1898 as the city’s main transportation hub, it’s now home to the Ferry Building Marketplace, where you’ll find everything from artisanal cheese at Cowgirl Creamery to fresh oysters at Hog Island Oyster Co 🦪

And hey, if you’re feeling fancy, you can always hit up [Verjus](https://www.verjuscave.com/ "") or [San Francisco Wine Society](https://www.sanfranciscowinesociety.com/ "") — two of my favorite wine bars downtown 🍷

**Main Takeaway**: If you’re looking for a central, well-connected place to stay in San Francisco, the Financial District is a solid pick. Especially for business travelers or those who love being near top restaurants, the Ferry Building, and easy transit options like BART and MUNI. It’s not the most “neighborhood-y” area, but it’s clean, safe, and considered one of the safest places to stay in San Francisco, with easy walking access to Union Square, Chinatown, and the Embarcadero.

## Where to Stay in San Francisco: The Richmond District

![](https://i.imgur.com/EVeYcVB.jpeg)

Annndddd last but not least — the beautiful, lovely, and oh so quiet San Francisco’s Richmond District!

This neighborhood is where fog meets flavor, packed with some of the city’s best dim sum, cozy cafes, and shockingly good Russian bakeries (yes, you need a piroshki).

You’re a short stroll from Golden Gate Park, the Presidio, and Ocean Beach, so whether you’re into museums, scenic hikes, or just staring dramatically at the Pacific, you’re covered.

Bonus: it’s waaaaay quieter than downtown, and you won’t have to dodge a million pigeons or robot taxis getting stuck on the streets.

### Where to stay in San Francisco’s Richmond District: Top vacation rental picks

There truly aren’t any hotels in The Richmond — that’s how residential it is. But there are some amazing gems on [Airbnb](https://www.airbnb.com/s/Richmond-District--San-Francisco--CA--USA/homes?refinement_paths%5B%5D=%2Fhomes&flexible_trip_lengths%5B%5D=one_week&monthly_start_date=2025-03-01&monthly_length=3&monthly_end_date=2025-06-01&price_filter_input_type=2&channel=EXPLORE&query=Richmond%20District%2C%20San%20Francisco%2C%20CA&place_id=ChIJK8HVABGHhYARPbkNZPtKm9E&date_picker_type=calendar&source=structured_search_input_header&search_type=user_map_move&search_mode=regular_search&price_filter_num_nights=5&ne_lat=37.79912721779363&ne_lng=-122.46639788803833&sw_lat=37.74566450094218&sw_lng=-122.49946211196169&zoom=14.359489793060387&zoom_level=14.359489793060387&search_by_map=true "") and [VRBO](https://vrbo.stay22.com/discoveroverthere/m0PcEI0r7E "") so I definitely recommend checking out both platforms for a quiet stay in a lovely Victorian.

![](https://i.imgur.com/6ku0Wyt.png)

### Things to do in the Richmond

The Richmond District is like your local San Francisco secret, packed with a little something for everyone.

Start with a buttery croissant from [Arsicault Bakery,](https://arsicault-bakery.com/ "") voted #1 croissant in San Francisco 🥐

After that, head over to Golden Gate Park to get your nature fix. Whether it’s wandering through the Japanese Tea Garden, geeking out at the California Academy of Sciences, or soaking in art at the de Young Museum.

Not enough fresh air? Hit up the Presidio for killer views of the Golden Gate Bridge or chill at Baker Beach. Oh, and the food scene? From next-level dim sum to Russian pastries, your taste buds are in for a treat.

I probably Doordash Asian food from the Richmond at least once a week. My absolute favorites are [B-Star](https://www.bstarbar.com/ "") (Burmese), [Mamahuhu](https://eatmamahuhu.com/ "")(Chinese), and [Kowloon Tong Dessert Cafe](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=4456&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.tripadvisor.com%2FRestaurant_Review-g60713-d3915791-Reviews-Kowloon_Tong_Dessert_Cafe-San_Francisco_California.html&trs=299090&journey_id=ejSW5wFL_lcNHEYWOe8nM&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") (HK style dessert).

**Main Takeaway:** Staying in the Richmond means getting the perfect mix of local charm and easy access to nature. Think quiet streets, cozy spots, and quick trips to Golden Gate Park and the coast. It’s also one of the safest places to stay in San Francisco, making it the ideal base for those who want to explore the city without the tourist crowds.

## San Francisco FAQ

Here are some commonly asked questions for first time visitors to San Francisco, California ☀️

![](https://i.imgur.com/hg9WiXP.jpeg)

### What areas should I avoid?

San Francisco is an incredible city, but like any major metro, there are a few areas you’ll want to steer clear of — mainly the **Tenderloin** and the stretch of **SoMa between 6th and 10th Street**.

These areas have higher crime rates, open-air drug use, and generally aren’t the best for walking around, especially at night.

The good news? SF is mostly made up of safe, walkable neighborhoods, and my guide focuses on the safest places to stay in San Francisco, steering you clear of any areas you’ll want to avoid.

### Do I need to rent a car in San Francisco?

![](https://i.imgur.com/rsWKxIO.jpeg)

[Renting a car](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=3555&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.discovercars.com%2Fusa-california%2Fsan-francisco%2Fsfo&trs=299090&journey_id=d8O0wdLYWbh33W1hvggjh&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") in San Francisco can sometimes be more of a hassle than a help. So I think it depends on whether or not you are visiting areas outside of the city. I’d definitely recommend it if you’re wanting to spend a couple days in wine country or drive down the coast to Monterey, Carmel, Big Sur, etc.

Then yes! Definitely [rent a car](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=3555&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.discovercars.com%2Fusa-california%2Fsan-francisco%2Fsfo&trs=299090&journey_id=2lr2vnHzaSjS_7cV5a1Ci&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner "") 🚘

But if you’re only planning on visiting San Francisco and/or seeing its immediate surrounding areas, then NO. I don’t think you will need or should rent a car. Since between expensive parking, confusing street signs, and the city’s (in)famous hills, you’re usually better off using public transit or uber/lyft/waymo.

But if you do [rent a car](https://emrldtp.com/re?marker=522542&p=3555&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.discovercars.com%2Fusa-california%2Fsan-francisco%2Fsfo&trs=299090&journey_id=r1hC84zuYUEz11-r5v2g-&trace_id=Zz25306174fc714d908c75f46-522542&promo_kind=tp_other&page_url=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveroverthere.com%2Fwhere-to-stay-in-san-francisco%2F&product_type=tp_manual&install_type=partner ""), just remember **one golden rule: never leave anything in the car.**

Car break-ins are unfortunately common, and thieves don’t discriminate. If they see a bag, jacket, or even an empty box, they’ll smash and grab.

So, if you must drive, keep the car completely empty when parked.

### What’s the best way to get around San Francisco?

Getting around San Francisco is a breeze if you know your options. And luckily for us, we have so many different methods of public transportation to get around. Including driver-less vehicles 🤖🚘

I guess we are at the forefront of technology so it makes sense.

- **Walking** – SF is a super walkable city (minus the hills), and most major attractions are within a few miles of each other
- **Muni (Buses & Light Rail)** – The cheapest way to get around, Muni covers the entire city with buses and streetcars. Just download the MuniMobile app for easy payment
- **Rideshares (Uber/Lyft/Waymo)** – Great for avoiding hills and late-night travel when public transit is less frequent
- **Biking & Scooters** – Rent a **Bay Wheels** bike or **Lime scooter** to cruise along the waterfront or through Golden Gate Park
- **Cable Cars**– A must-do at least once! The Powell-Hyde and Powell-Mason lines are the most scenic
- **Ferries** – Heading to Sausalito or Alcatraz? The ferry is the way to go, with stunning views of the bay
- **BART (Bay Area Rapid Transit)** – Best for getting to/from the airport or hopping between SF and the East Bay

### How long do you recommend staying in San Francisco?

I think 3-4 days is the perfect amount of time to experience most of what San Francisco has to offer. For a complete itinerary, check out my guide on [how to spend 3 unforgettable days in San Francisco (w/ sample itinerary)](https://discoveroverthere.com/3-day-san-francisco-itinerary/ "").

I also created this [local’s 3-day guide on Thatch](https://www.thatch.co/guide/kc5qnoxv33mh/edit "") that has all of my favorite spots pinned on a map 🗺️

## Safest Areas to Stay in San Francisco: Final Thoughts

![](https://i.imgur.com/YhUVYnz.jpeg)

So, here’s the deal: San Francisco is a total gem, and there’s no reason to let the mainstream media scare you off. The city is packed with safe, vibrant, and fun neighborhoods that easily make it one of the safest places to stay in San Francisco!

Whether you’re crashing in Union Square, soaking in the Marina girlie (or guy) vibes, or living your best life in Nob Hill. There’s always something to do, from exploring Fort Mason to checking out iconic spots like the Golden Gate Bridge, or indulging in insane food🍴

Sure, no place is perfect, but with a little insider knowledge, you’ll find that San Francisco is full of welcoming areas to stay, play, and eat your heart out.

Don’t overthink it. San Francisco is a fabulous, safe area to visit, and you’re going to love it 🌁

Title: San Francisco's Neighborhoods: Top Picks by Globalphile
[Skip to content](https://globalphile.com/san-francisco-neighborhoodsdistricts/#content)

San Francisco’s neighborhoods include:

Nob Hill: This is a great area of the city with stately homes and high-rise apartment buildings. I have stayed several times at the [Fairmont](https://www.fairmont.com/en/hotels/san-francisco/fairmont-heritage-place-ghirardelli-square.html) which I really like. I prefer staying in the old building from 1907, with its great character, rather than in the newer tower from 1961.

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-201-of-216.jpg)Nob Hill The Fairmont

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-197-of-216.jpg)Nob Hill

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-202-of-216.jpg)Nob Hill

Across the street is the InterContinental Mark Hopkins with its famous bar [Top of the Mark](http://topofthemark.com/), an Art Deco bar. I always like watching the cable cars as they go up and down the steep hills of Nob Hill.

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-24-of-125.jpg)Nob Hill

Union Square: I have also stayed in the Union Square area several times which is a very convenient location from which to explore the city. I recently stayed at the hip [Vertigo Hotel](http://www.hotelvertigosf.com/) at 940 Sutter. This location is in lower Nob Hill and close to Union Square. It is part of the Oxford Capital Hotel Group which has several boutique hotels in San Francisco each with its own character and personality. The Vertigo was a great value. It now has a new cafe in the lobby.

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-56-of-216.jpg)Union Square

Union Square is the main shopping area. My favorite store to explore is the San Francisco based [Gump’s](http://www.gumps.com/), at 250 Post St., for its unique home accessories, table top and home furnishings. The store is under new management and is much improved. You should stop at Ghiradelli for their chocolates, at Nespresso Cafe for a cup of coffee and see the shops behind Gump’s on Maiden Lane.

The Financial District is just east of Union Square. This is the location of my favorite dim sum restaurant, [Yank Sing](https://yanksing.com/) at 101 Spear St., which I have been to at least three times. It recently received the Michelin Bib Gourmand designation.

Alamo Square: On my previous visit, I played tourist and went a little west of downtown to Alamo Square. The area has great Victorian architecture. The row of houses facing the park on Steiner Street, known as the Painted Ladies, are often shown in the foreground of panoramic pictures of the city’s downtown.

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-21-of-2161.jpg)Alamo Square

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-25-of-216.jpg)Alamo Square

Civic Center: This is the area just south of Union Square. Here I explored the [Asian Art Museum](http://www.asianart.org/), at 200 Larkin, for the first time. I learned about the museum several years ago when it was the recipient of Llloyd Cotsen’s amazing Japanese bamboo basket collection. I had seen wonderful traveling exhibitions from the collection in Aspen and Chicago and had started a small collection myself of these contemporary bamboo pieces from the same gallery in Santa Fe. There are a few examples from the collection on display.

In addition, there are wonderful stone carvings from Southeast Asia; bronzes, pottery and jade from China; scrolls, ceramics and decorative arts from Japan and Buddhist religious art from Nepal, Tibet and Bhutan. The collection is really outstanding and the number of pieces is quite overwhelming. Check the website for special exhibitions. I just missed one on objects from Bali. There is a nice museum shop and café where you can grab lunch or a cup of coffee or tea.

South of Market (SOMA) and [Yerba Buena Gardens](http://www.yerbabuenagardens.com/): I ventured into this area for the first time, this trip, as I wanted to explore this emerging area. It is home to many museums, the convention center, performing arts center, a children’s center and a shopping and entertainment complex.

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-72-of-216.jpg)South of Market SOMA

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-67-of-216.jpg)South of Market SOMA

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-100-of-216.jpg)South of Market (SOMA)

My goal, however, was to visit the [San Francisco Museum of Modern Art](http://www.sfmoma.org/) at 151 3rd St. The building, designed by Swiss architect Mario Botta with huge skylight, was attractive with several floors of exhibition space and a rooftop sculpture garden. I enjoyed viewing the permanent collection with works by Henri Matisse, Georges Braque, Diego Rivera and Frida Kahlo, Jackson Pollack, Clyfford Still, Picasso, Jasper Johns, Roy Lichtenstein, Robert Rauschenberg, Georgia O’Keeffe, Mark Rothko and others.

[Golden Gate Park](https://sfrecpark.org/770/Golden-Gate-Park): I highly recommend Golden Gate Park. This is a three mile long park in the western part of the city. The park was started in the 1870’s to compete with such parks as Central Park in New York. Here I visited the famous [de Young Museum](http://deyoung.famsf.org/) at 50 Hagiwara Tea Garden Drive. After the 1989 earthquake, the museum was torn down and totally rebuilt in 2005.  I enjoyed a special Picasso exhibition from the Picasso Museum in Paris. I also enjoyed the permanent collection which features American art with works by John Singer Sargent, Mary Cassatt and Grant Wood; art of the Americas, African art, Oceanic art and Textile art. This is a great museum that should not be missed.

Also not to be missed is the [Japanese Tea Garden](http://japaneseteagardensf.com/). This is a maze of winding paths, stone lanterns, ornamental ponds, a wooden pagoda, a Zen garden and wooden tea house built for the Mid-winter Fair of 1894. This is a perfect place to relax after visiting the de Young. I would eat here rather than at the museum.

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-49-of-120.jpg)Golden Gate Park Japanese Tea Garden

Across form the de Young is the [California Academy of Sciences](http://www.calacademy.org/?utm_expid=12551229-31.Z5QmE7CSRWmG4C8fP4hc2Q.0&utm_referrer=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.google.com%2F) with its contemporary design by world famous architect Renzo Piano. On the day I was there the park was crowded. There was music, dancing and food trucks offering food for those enjoying a rare sunny, warm summer day.

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-67-of-120.jpg)Golden Gate Park California Academy of Sciences

Marina District: I really enjoy this area of the city. It has a great neighborhood feel. It was heavily damaged by the earthquake in 1989 where the ground liquefied during the tremors. All is now erased and the neighborhood is thriving. I like the strip along Chestnut with its many restaurants, cafes, coffee shops, boutiques and food markets.

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-63-of-125.jpg)Marina District

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-53-of-125.jpg)Marina District

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-48-of-125.jpg)Marina District

I also like the part of the Marina District known as Cow Hollow. Along Union Street between Van Ness and Steiner was a great group of galleries, boutiques and restaurants along with some national chain specialty stores. From here I drove down Fillmore Street through the Pacific Heights area. This is another great area to explore with great shops and restaurants. I need to go back and explore these two areas more on my next trip.

Hayes Valley: Having seen the Hayes Valley neighborhood on recent trips, I explored this fun neighborhood. It is a hip, young neighborhood with many boutiques, shops, restaurants, food trucks, coffee and ice cream shops. The small square on Hayes west of Gough, Patricia’s Green, has a small square where the locals enjoy sitting out in the great sunshine with a coffee or ice cream.  I particularly love the coffee stand in a garage in an alley! The neighborhood is north and south of Hayes between Webster and Franklin.

[Japantown](http://sfjapantown.org/): This is the center of the Japanese-American cultural life. There is Japan Center with galleries, shops, restaurants and cinemas and a large Peace Pagoda rising above the plaza.

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-46-of-216.jpg)Japan Town

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-49-of-216.jpg)Japan Town

North Beach: Near Powell and Union, this a fun neighborhood, with tons of cafes, restaurants, bars and shops. This is one of the city’s oldest neighborhoods that sits between Russian Hill, Telegraph Hill and Fisherman’s Wharf. You can hang out with the locals in Washington Square Park. Next time I will consider staying at the [**Washington Square Inn**](https://www.wsisf.com/) at 1660 Stockton St. This is a small, charming B&B right on the park.

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-211-of-216.jpg)Russian Hill

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-213-of-216.jpg)Russian Hill

Castro District: I enjoyed exploring the Castro district for the first time which is the gay area that is so famous. I liked the colors, murals and the neighborhood feel.

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-112-of-125.jpg)Castro District

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-107-of-125.jpg)Castro District

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-104-of-125.jpg)Castro District

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-99-of-125.jpg)Castro District

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-76-of-125.jpg)Castro District

The Mission: On my last trip I spent a large amount of time exploring this area south of Market along Mission, Valencia plus Folsom and S. Van Ness Ave. There are many great bars, restaurants and some interesting shops and boutiques. It quickly became one of my favorite areas of the city.

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-59-of-1251.jpg)Marina District

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-81-of-125.jpg)Castro District

Next time I want to focus on the Presidio,  a 1,500-acre park on a former military post.

![](https://globalphile.s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/untitled-99-of-120.jpg)The Presidio
